I've been a vet tech & worked in rescues on & off for over 12 years now and have seen soo many cases where it's being over used or not used right. If it's used more than half power more than like twice a day their will without question always be a patchy area with hairl loss, burns to the area and the prongs sometimes break the skin and even cause infection and discoloration.  But if used correctly, meaning you try the levels on yourself first to know how it feels (even though dogs have tougher skin than humans, and many have a undercoat or double under coat and medium to long hair too, and they don't have pores like us)  so however it feels when you test it on yourself, it'll be slightly less for them, also if it's not too tight, and the prongs ALWAYS come with rubber type cap to put over them so it's not just metal on the dogs neck, and most always come with a beep, vibrate and shock mode and many are sound activated, so when the barking volume reaches a certain level it will beep 3 times, vibrate then bee 3-6times and then shock once or twice then repeat. Also there's many levels to them.   No taking up for him, but in my years of experience people get pretty dramatic and upset about them. High voltage generators produce a lot of electrical noise that can be picked by every bit of audio equipment (there's shielding, but it can only do so much, that's why it's quieter). Shock collars are not cruel or painful at all when used properly.  When set properly they are nothing more than a gentle tingle to get your dog's attention.  They are an invaluable training tool for anybody serious about dog training.    I use one for my dog.  He's never yelped in pain.  I can put his collar on my neck and hold the button down and "shock" myself without discomfort.  And human skin is much thinner and more sensitive than the skin on a dog's neck.   That being said, hasan is not using the collar correctly.  He has it set way too high and is not using it appropriately at all.  1. Shock collars are a tool, not a permanent collar.  They shouldn't be used more than 2 or 3 hours a day.   2. When set properly, the shock is not painful at all.  It is a gentle tingle.   3. The shock collar is not supposed to be used as a punishment.  It is used just to get the dog's attention when it is ignoring commands and focused on something else.   4. Anybody serious about dog training, especially for working or hunting dogs that engage in off leash activities where the dog must obey 100% of the time for their own safety, uses shock collars.  When the coyotes show up, or the dog is running towards traffic, you need to be able to call them back 100% of the time.  A shock collar is the best way to train that.    5. You should really do some research and learn about things before you go off half cocked.  Implying that shock collars are cruel, even though you know absolutely nothing about them is just dumb, and only serves to demonize good people who use them the right way.
